## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: The task models the instantaneous population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and current population size P, a central problem in population ecology. The relationship typically involves per-capita growth rate forms (multiplicative factor on P), density-dependent regulation (saturation, Allee effects), and possibly time-varying environmental forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited intrinsic growth)
- Logistic (Verhulst) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (density-dependent saturation to carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 + c2 * log(c3 * P)) (multiplicative log dependency, decelerating growth)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized density regulation shape)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (cubic with two internal equilibria)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - c2 * P**c3) (flexible asymmetric growth curve)
- Logistic with constant harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 (constant removal rate)
- Logistic with proportional harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P (density-independent mortality)
- Time-decaying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(-c2 * t)) (environmentally degrading habitat)
- Exponential decay growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * t) (intrinsic growth declining over time)
- von Bertalanffy growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (allometric anabolism minus catabolism)
- Logistic with sinusoidal forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (seasonally forced growth)
- Cubic density-dependent mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P**3 (higher-order density regulation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Low-density exponential growth: dominant linear term c0*P when P is small, giving unbounded increase
- Logistic saturation: negative quadratic term -c1*P**2 causing growth to halt at equilibrium P = c0/c1
- Allee effect: cubic shape dP/dt changes sign twice, implying positive growth only between lower and upper thresholds
- Gompertz log-dependence: growth rate per capita decays as c*log(P), capturing slower-than-logistic decline at high density
- Time-dependent environment: explicit t in factor multiplying P or P**2 represents gradually changing carrying capacity
- Harvesting/mortality offset: constant negative term or negative linear term in P added to otherwise logistic growth
- Allometric scaling in growth: power-law P**c1 with c1 ≠ 1 suggests metabolic scaling of production vs. size-dependent loss
- Seasonal forcing: additive sinusoidal term with time argument models periodic environmental fluctuation
- Threshold activation: factor (P - c) enforces zero growth below critical density, characteristic of Allee or depensation effects
- Accelerating density dependence: cubic term -c*P**3 steepens decline at high densities beyond simple logistic

To match GT’s static part \(\frac{A P^2}{C P + 1}\), choose \(c_4 = C\), \(c_0 = A/C\), and \(c_3 = -A/C\) (so the \(P\) term vanishes). The dynamic part matches by choosing \(c_1 = A\), \(c_2 = -B\).  
**Perfect match found.** → Match.

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT:** `0.3156*P*exp(-0.05405*t) + 0.3156*P²/(9.871*P + 1)`

Let me analyze the structure. The GT has two terms:
1. `c0*P*exp(-c1*t)` — a term proportional to P times a decaying exponential in t
2. `c2*P²/(c4*P + c5)` — a rational function of P (specifically P²/(aP+b))

Now I need to check which candidates can reproduce this structure exactly.

**Key observation:** The second GT term `P²/(aP+b)` can be rewritten. Let me do partial fractions:
`P²/(aP+b) = P/a - b/(a²) + b²/(a²(aP+b))`

Or equivalently: `P²/(aP+b) = (1/a)*P - b/a² + (b/a)²·1/(aP+b)`

So the GT can be written as:
`c0*P*exp(-c1*t) + α*P + β + γ/(aP+b)`

where α, β, γ are constants derived from the partial fraction decomposition.

Also note: `log(1 + c/P) = log((P+c)/P) = log(P+c) - log(P)`. This is NOT equivalent to `1/(aP+b)` or `P/(aP+b)`.

So candidates using `log(1+c/P)` need that term to vanish (coefficient = 0), and they need another mechanism to produce `P²/(aP+b)`.

Let me check candidates that have the rational function `P²/(aP+b)` or `P*c/(P*c+c)` structure:

**Candidates with `P*c/(P*c+c)` or `P²/(P*c+c)` terms:**

Let me note that `P²/(aP+b)` can also be written as `P·[P/(aP+b)]`, so a term like `P*c3/(P*c4+c5)` gives `c3*P/(c4*P+c5)`, which is NOT the same as `P²/(aP+b)` unless we factor differently. Actually `P²/(aP+b) = (1/a)·P·(aP)/(aP+b) = (1/a)·P·[1 - b/(aP+b)]` ... Let me reconsider.

`c3*P/(c4*P+c5)` — this is `c3*P/(c4*P+c5)`. We need `P²/(aP+b)`. These differ: one is degree 1/1 rational, the other is degree 2/1.

But if a candidate has BOTH `P*c0` (linear in P) AND `P*c3/(P*c4+c5)`, can we combine them?

`c0*P + c3*P/(c4*P+c5) = P*[c0*(c4*P+c5) + c3]/(c4*P+c5) = P*[c0*c4*P + c0*c5 + c3]/(c4*P+c5)`

This gives `(c0*c4*P² + (c0*c5+c3)*P)/(c4*P+c5)`.

For this to equal `α*P²/(c4*P+c5)`, we need `c0*c5+c3 = 0`, i.e., `c3 = -c0*c5`. Then we get `c0*c4*P²/(c4*P+c5)`. Yes! This works.

So candidates with structure: `P*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P*c3/(P*c4+c5) + [extra terms that can be zeroed]` can match.

Also, candidates with explicit `P²*c0/(P*c1+c2)` can directly provide the rational term.

Let me also check: can `log(1+c/P)` be set to zero? Yes, by setting its coefficient to 0.

Now let me systematically go through candidates:

Match: c5=D, c6=1, c0*c5=B → c0=B/D, c0*c6=c0=B/D ≠ 0. But GT needs the P coefficient to be 0 (no non-exponential P term in numerator). So c0*c6 = B/D ≠ 0, but GT has 0 for the non-exponential P coefficient. Contradiction!

Unless... GT numerator: `B*P² + A*D*P²*exp + A*P*exp`. The non-exponential P coefficient IS 0. But candidate gives c0*c6 for non-exponential P coefficient. So c0*c6=0. If c6=0, denominator = c5*P, and we get `c0*P + c7/(c5*P)` which has 1/P term. If c0=0, then c0*c5=0≠B. No match.
